SHARPER PROOF FRAMING (derived this turn): g bad ⟺ ∃ deg<n/2 poly c with f(x):=c(x) - g x^{n/2} - x^{3n/4} having ≥5n/8 roots in μ_n. f has degree 3n/4, support {0..n/2-1, n/2, 3n/4}. ≥5n/8 roots in μ_n ⟹ f = g_T(x)·h(x) where g_T = Π_{t∈T}(x-t) | (x^n-1), deg g_T=5n/8 (T = 5n/8-subset of μ_n), deg h = n/8. The CONSTRAINT: f=g_T·h must have ZERO coefficients at degrees {n/2+1,...,3n/4-1} (n/4-1 conditions), coeff -1 at 3n/4, and coeff at n/2 = -g (free, determines g). So B(n) = #{distinct g arising from factorizations g_T·h (g_T | x^n-1 deg 5n/8, h deg n/8) with the n/4-1 middle coeffs vanishing}. This is a CLEAN coefficient-vanishing / divisibility count — the right object for an error-locator/generating-function proof of the plateau. n=8 transient: at n=8 the "middle" {n/2+1..3n/4-1} is empty (n/4-1=1, degrees {5,6}? n=8: n/2=4,3n/4=6, middle {5}=1 condition) — the constraint structure degenerates at small n.
CAMPAIGN L1-L82. State: B(n)=2-sparse-syndrome coset count (validated 8,16 by 2 methods); plateau O(n)=9 verified n=16,32, UNPROVEN, n>=64 infeasible (list-regime hardness); sharp f=g_T·h factorization framing for the proof.

## L87 (bulk supports GROW but are SELF-SIMILAR under doubling; support-confinement REFUTED; decimation/value-bijection is the route) 2026-06-19
The earlier bulk workflow (woo9s2ztr) finished with a strong synthesis (independent dual-syndrome exhaustive verification, p=1009): B(8)=20,B(16)=36 re-confirmed. NEW FINDINGS:
- **support-confinement REFUTED:** bulk minimal error supports have weight EXACTLY 3n/8, GROWING with n (3,6,12 at n=8,16,32). So the bulk is NOT a fixed-size error structure. (My L-earlier "fixed structure" angle (a) is dead.)
- **SELF-SIMILARITY (key new structure):** several bulk supports are doubling-self-similar: E = E_half ∪ (E_half + n/2). E.g. g=56: E={0,1,3}∪({0,1,3}+8); g=101: {0,2,3}∪({0,2,3}+8). So the support at level a+1 = (support at level a) ∪ (shift by n/2) — a clean doubling map.
- **PRECISE REMAINING LEMMA:** N_bulk(a) = #bulk orbits = 8 for a>=4, =4 for a=3 (count stabilizes though supports/modulus grow). The gain-stops "+4 at a=3->4, +0 after".
- **ROUTE (matches my running workflow we7uhkigm):** the value-level decimation x->x^4 reducing f=g_T*h to fixed-size mu_4-graded blocks, proving the g-VALUE count is independent of #blocks (=a) for a>=4. NOT support-confinement (refuted); NOT a-priori saturation (scale-invariance is a genuine obstruction); must be EARNED by an explicit finite-rank/bijection mechanism on g-VALUES.
CONFIRMS the decimation workflow is correctly aimed; the self-similar support structure E=E_half∪(E_half+n/2) is the explicit doubling map the bijection should use. Still OPEN; the decimation reduction to a fixed g-value count is the live closable route. CAMPAIGN L1-L87.

## L88 (decimation "mostly-4-periodic" conjecture REFUTED unanimously; bulk uses n-growing frequencies; bad-prime split refined) 2026-06-19

- **"bulk solution forces c mostly-4-periodic (non-r=0 coupling coeffs confined to a FIXED finite set of r)" is FALSE.** Restricting the explaining poly c to the 4-periodic frequencies {0,1,N,N+1} at n=16 recovers ONLY the 4 SPECIAL orbits, NOT the 32 bulk. - The mu_4-DILATION symmetry (size-4 orbits) IS proven and n-independent, but that only organizes the count into orbits, doesn't BOUND it.
- The decimation reduces "g bad" to a coupled-RS-decoding with the FIXED mu_4 matrix [1,i4^j], BUT the per-r free pairs (c_r, c_{r+M}) range over an n-GROWING index set — so the system has M-dependent dimension. No M-independent count follows.
- **NEW (bad-prime refinement):** p-independence is NOT literal even for good-scale primes: B(16)=36 at GENERIC primes (97,193,353) but 32 at sporadic small bad primes (measured 113, 257) where "Family B" (4 of the bulk orbits) is lost. Correct statement: "B(n)=36 for n>=16 at all but a finite set of bad primes." (Consistent with the campaign's good/bad-prime convention; the n=8 disc was 2^41*17^2*257^2 — 113 is a NEW bad prime for n=16.)
HONEST STATUS: the bulk-8 stabilization is OPEN and my best concrete reduction (4-periodic decimation) is now REFUTED. What stands: special orbit (4) proven n-independent (airtight, 3 constructions); anchors B(8,16,32)=20,36,36 (now incl exhaustive dual-syndrome); bulk supports self-similar E=E_half∪(E_half+n/2) (L87) but using growing frequencies (L88, so the half-blocks scale). Treat B(32)=36 as STRONGLY-evidenced, not certified.]

- **THE OPEN LEMMA (Bulk Freeze, exact):** #{g: exists c with sum_j #{v in mu_{n/4}: P_j(v) != v_j(g)} <= 3n/8} = 32 for all n=2^a>=16, where P_j(v)=sum_r zeta^{jr}(c_r+i4^j c_{r+m})v^r, v_j(g)=i4^{3j}+g i4^{2j}. This is the original n-indexed problem in disguise — NOT reduced to finite size.
STATUS: bulk stabilization OPEN; all candidate mechanisms refuted (support-confinement L87, 4-periodic decimation L88/L89, Galois/Lam-Leung/chi^2 earlier); my K1/K0 framing corrected; B(32)=36 downgraded to strongly-evidenced-not-certified. ## L92 (T5/T2-4 "finite D4-type of v-tuple" REFUTED analytically — v-tuple carries 1 dof = g) 2026-06-19
Tested the convergent core of the highest-promise invented tools (T5 nov=10, T2-4, B4-T2, T4): the bulk-orbit "type" = a finite n-independent D4-class of the per-class constant 4-tuple (v_0,v_1,v_2,v_3). REFUTED by elementary algebra (no computation needed). With i4=primitive 4th root (i4^2=-1, i4^3=-i4, i4^4=1):
  v_j = i4^{3j} + g·i4^{2j}  =>  v_0=1+g, v_1=-i4-g, v_2=-1+g, v_3=i4-g.
So v_0-v_2 = 2 and v_1-v_3 = -2i4 are CONSTANTS (independent of g), and v_0+v_2 = 2g. The v-tuple is an AFFINE BIJECTIVE encoding of the single scalar g — it carries EXACTLY 1 degree of freedom, = g itself. Therefore a "finite D4-type of the v-tuple" CANNOT distinguish the 36 distinct bad-g; the type-set is not finite-and-informative, it's a relabeling of g. The decimation transfer operator's proposed FINITE state space (the v_j-state) is VACUOUS. **T5/T2-4/B4-T2/T4 (the whole "finite v-state automaton/zeta" cluster) REFUTED.** The bad/not-bad distinction lives in the EXPLAINING POLY structure (the n-growing coupled coefficients c_r), NOT in the 4 class-constants v_j — consistent with L88/L89 (bulk uses n-growing frequencies). The freeze, if real, is NOT a finite-v-state phenomenon.
SURVIVING untested invented tools (not yet refuted): T1 self-similar Wronskian descent (co-restriction of the explaining poly, the n-growing part); T2/T2-2 quadratic frequency-FOLDING (fold the explaining poly's n-growing freqs under x->x^2, NOT the v-constants); B4-T4 g-value doubling-lift bijection; T2-5 Smith-form normal form of the per-block decimation module; B4-T1 resultant R_a(g) degree as discrete invariant. These act on the EXPLAINING POLY / resultant (the right object per L92), not the v-tuple. 
META: invent->test->refute working as intended; killed the top-promise tool by elementary algebra (provably-doesn't-work). The freeze must come from the n-growing explaining-poly coupling, not any finite class-constant state. CAMPAIGN L1-L92.

## L105 (RESOLVED off-BGK-vs-BGK: it is a finite HEIGHT BOUND, NOT a √p wall — the L103 "reduces to BGK" was MISFRAMED) 2026-06-20
Exact reasoning (mine, /tmp/pgwork) resolves the L103/L104 central question: the off-BGK closure is GENUINELY a finite height bound, NOT the BGK √p wall. The agent's "reduces to BGK (√p root count)" was MISFRAMED.
**THE ARGUMENT (exact, clean):** the band defect condition is e_k(E)=0 for all k in {n/8+1,..,n/4-1}, where E=μ_n∖A is the ERROR SET. Crucially e_k(E) is the elementary symmetric function of the roots in E — a FIXED CYCLOTOMIC INTEGER per E, with **NO g-dependence** in the band condition (g is determined afterward, or the condition is purely on E). The number of adjacent error-sets E is a FIXED combinatorial count (binomial, p-INDEPENDENT: 2304 at n=16). Therefore:
  bad-prime set B(n) = ∪_{adjacent E} { primes p | N(e_band(E)) } = a FINITE union of finite sets = FINITE, enumerable p-INDEPENDENTLY.
So #defect-g ≤ #adjacent-E = O_n(1), BOUNDED in p. The count does NOT grow with p ⟹ it is NOT a √p character-sum wall in the count sense. This is exactly L97-P1 (B(n) = divisors of ∏N(Δ_A), finite), re-confirmed and now sharpened: the band condition has no g, so it's purely a height question on FIXED cyclotomic integers.
**THE CORRECT REMAINING QUESTION (off-BGK, not BGK):** is max B(n) < n^4, i.e. is the largest prime ≡1 mod n dividing any N(e_band(E)) below n^4, uniformly in a? This is a HEIGHT/SIZE bound on cyclotomic resultant norms — genuinely off-BGK (no sup-norm η_b anywhere; it's about |N(e_band(E))| and its prime factorization). VERIFIED: n=16 max=17<n^4; n=32 known bad primes {97,193,257,1153} all <n^4=1048576.
**SO THE OFF-BGK ROUTE DOES NOT COLLAPSE TO BGK** (correcting L103's worry): the closure is a height bound on FIXED cyclotomic integers e_band(E), a finite p-independent object — categorically different from BGK's p-dependent sup-norm. The agent conflated "F_p-roots of R_m(g)" (a g-polynomial framing) with the correct "p | N(e_band(E))" (no g, fixed integer) framing; the latter is manifestly finite/height.
HONEST STATUS: off-BGK route INTACT (does not reduce to BGK). Floor closed n=16. Open = the uniform height bound max_E max{p≡1 mod n : p|N(e_band(E))} < n^4 for all a — a clean, finite-per-n, genuinely-off-BGK Diophantine statement on elementary-symmetric cyclotomic integers. Decisive workflow running to nail the height-growth empirically. CAMPAIGN L1-L105.

## L106 (DECISIVE, EXACT: off-BGK closure IS a finite HEIGHT BOUND — 0-dimensional variety, flat count in p, g LINEAR; does NOT reduce to BGK) 2026-06-20
The decisive workflow (6 agents, EXACT computation, all validated against g=71@p=97 anchor) UNANIMOUSLY verdicts off-BGK-height-bound, with the structural proof:
**(1) g enters LINEARLY** — g is solely the coefficient of the x^{n/2} column; the matching system Σc_k x^k - g x^{n/2} = x^{3n/4} on A is LINEAR in (c_0..c_{n/2-1}, g). So bad-ness is NOT a high-degree-polynomial root count in g. (Refutes the "R_m(g) high-degree => √p roots" framing at the root.) Per-E forced-g is SUBSINGLETON (<=1), matching the in-tree incidence_subsingleton lemma.

## L112 (unifying scheme idea REFUTED; part (B) = uniform-k lemma; NEW VERIFIED v2-stratification lead → Stickelberger) 2026-06-20
The unifying-idea workflow (18 attempts, 0 airtight) honestly REFUTED the single-scheme closure AND surfaced a genuinely-new verified lead:
- **UNIFYING SCHEME IDEA REFUTED:** "all bad primes = disc(X/Z) primes" is FALSE — band primes have Q8 FULLY SPLIT (4 roots, separable, disc≠0 mod p), so they are NOT disc primes; the band ideal e_k(E)=0 has n/8-1 GROWING conditions (3,7,15,31 at n=32,64,128,256), so X is a FAMILY X_a not a fixed Z-scheme ⟹ "disc(X/Z)" ill-posed. Part (A) and (B) are genuinely DIFFERENT objects; no single disc/height idea closes both. (Also the flagged trap: |disc|<bound bounds the NUMBER of bad primes, never the LARGEST; and the e_k height 2^{3n/8} EXPLODES past n² at n=64.)
- **PART (B) = THE UNIFORM-k LEMMA (exact):** band primes satisfy k:=(p-1)/n < n (⟺ p<n²). Razor-thin: max band prime 929=29·32+1, k=29=90.6% of n=32. No non-explicit height bound can close a 9% gap; needs an EXPLICIT k<n mechanism.
- **NEW VERIFIED LEAD (v2-stratification, genuinely new, I verified):** band primes have v2(p-1) ∈ {a, a+1} EXACTLY (n=32: all band v2∈{5,6}; n=16: bad 17 has v2=4=a). Primes with v2(p-1)≥a+2 (128|p-1 at n=32: 641,769,1153,1409) split Q8 but are NOT band-bad — the extra 2-adic depth DISSOLVES the defect. So band realizability FORCES 2-adic depth = a or a+1. This is a Stickelberger/Gauss-sum 2-adic-valuation phenomenon: the band condition e_k(E)=0 among 2n-th roots is a vanishing-Gauss/Jacobi-sum condition whose prime support is governed by Stickelberger's factorization, with a 2-adic-depth filtration.
**MOST PROMISING DISTANT MACHINERY for the uniform-k lemma (part B, the entire remaining open):** (1) Stickelberger + 2-adic stratification of Gauss/Jacobi sums on μ_{2n} (the v2-split points here; Stickelberger bounds primes by ideal-norms = genuine étale/discriminant statement for the growing-but-cyclotomically-structured band scheme, could give k<n); (2) class-field/Kummer tower with explicit CONDUCTOR (conductor bounds largest prime, often n-smooth); (3) a genuine 4n↔n band recursion (FFT-graded e_k doubling, analogous to in-tree E6 #bad_{2n}=#bad_n) for explicit uniform k<n.
HONEST STATUS: part (A) PROVEN (A1, verified, disc primes {17,257}<n² uniform); part (B) OPEN = the uniform-k lemma (band primes have k<n), with a NEW verified v2∈{a,a+1} stratification pointing at Stickelberger. The /goal's single-complete-idea is NOT met — part (B) is a genuine open Diophantine lemma, but now sharply stated (k<n) with a concrete new mechanism (2-adic Gauss-sum stratification). NOT closure; real new verified structure. CAMPAIGN L1-L112.

## L113 (LITERATURE RESEARCH done + uniform-k lemma SHARPENED to a verified structural form: oddpart(p-1)<n ∧ v2∈{a,a+1}) 2026-06-20
Did genuine literature retrieval (arXiv API; WebSearch down) for part (B) — doc docs/kb/literature-uniform-k-lemma-2026-06-20.md. The band condition e_k(E)=0 IS a vanishing-sum-of-roots-of-unity problem; governing literature:
- **Lam-Leung "vanishing sums of m-th roots of unity in FINITE fields" (math/9605216):** the weight set W_p(m) = which p,N admit a vanishing sum of N m-th roots in F_p. A NEW mod-p relation of length L needs p ≤ L; but L=C(3n/8,k)>>n^2, so this alone is too weak.
- **Poonen-Rubinstein / Christie-Dykema-Klep (2008.11268):** minimal-vanishing-sum classification ≤ weight 21.
- **All, "Gauss Sums, Stickelberger's Theorem..." (1502.01578):** Stickelberger Galois annihilators via Gauss sums — the route the v2-stratification points to.
- **"Cyclotomic polynomials at roots of unity" (1611.06783), Kumar-Kumar power sums (1503.07281), Laba-Marshall (2202.07555).**
HONEST GAP from literature: Mahler/Hadamard bounds give the SIZE |N(e_k(E))| not the LARGEST prime factor; Lam-Leung length-bound too weak; Stickelberger is the right machinery but no off-the-shelf theorem closes THIS resultant.
**SHARPENED uniform-k lemma (verified structural form, NEW):** ALL bad primes n=32 have oddpart(p-1) < n=32 (oddparts ∈{1,3,7,9,11,21,29}) AND v2(p-1) ∈ {a-1,a,a+1} (disc 17:v2=4, 257:v2=8 outlier(=2a-2); band v2∈{5,6}={a,a+1}). For band primes: v2=a ⟹ k=oddpart<n; v2=a+1 ⟹ k=2·oddpart, oddpart<n/2. Either way p-1 = 2^{v2}·oddpart < 2^a·n = n² ⟹ **p < n² follows from {v2∈{a,a+1}} ∧ {oddpart<n}**. Both verified at n=16,32. So part (B) = prove these two 2-adic/odd-structure constraints on band primes, via Stickelberger/Gauss-sum valuation of the band resultant.
STATUS (honest, addressing the /goal): literature research DONE (condition 3); part (B) SHARPENED to a clean verified 2-adic+odd structural conjecture with the right machinery (Lam-Leung+Stickelberger) identified. NOT closed — part (B) is a genuine open cyclotomic-resultant smoothness lemma; the standard literature gives size not largest-prime, and the Stickelberger application to THIS resultant is genuinely new mathematics not in the library. The single-complete-idea is not achievable in-session because part (B) is open research, now stated as sharply as the structure allows. CAMPAIGN L1-L113.

The floor-RELEVANT (freeze-BREAKING, list GROWS) deviations are UP only: n=16 has NONE >36 except the full-group p=17 (degenerate); n=32 p=97 (+12, =smallest prime ≡1 mod 32). 
**CLEAN CLOSURE STRUCTURE (emerging):** (1) the defect-CORE polynomial R_n is smooth (disc small-prime: {2,3} at n=16; {2,17,257} at n=32 — the odd primes are FERMAT, tower-invariant, PROVABLY bounded via composition-discriminant A1 + disc(S)=2-power + S(0)=±3^4). ## L125 (REFRAME: disc-height bound DEAD (cyclotomic primes ~2^{n/2}); floor reduces to ONE crisp degree question — does the adjacent/7th-type add p-dependent bad-g beyond the FIXED deg-36 locus?) 2026-06-21
**(1) disc primes are CYCLOTOMIC-EVALUATION primes** p | Φ_{ord_p(2)}(2): at n=16, 3=Φ_2(2), 7=Φ_3(2), 17=Φ_8(2), 257=Φ_16(2), 113|Φ_28(2). The ones ≡1 mod 16 have d=ord_p(2)∈{8,16,28}. The STRUCTURAL prime is Φ_n(2)=2^{n/2}+1 (d=n ⟹ p≡1 mod n). It GROWS like 2^{n/2}: 257(@16)<n^4, 65537(@32)<n^4, 6700417(@64)<n^4, but 2^64+1's factor 67280421310721(@128) >> n^4=2.68e8. ⟹ **TARGET-1 ("all disc primes ≡1 mod n < n^4") is FALSE for n≥128.** The disc-HEIGHT bound is DEAD.
**(2) BUT these large primes are DOWN (benign).** 257=Φ_16(2) gives B=32<36 at n=16. So large disc primes do NOT break the floor — they're root-collision (DOWN) primes.
**(3) THE DEGREE ARGUMENT (key).** Dilation symmetry = C4 (g→i·g), FIXED for all n ⟹ orbit-invariant = g^4 ⟹ R_n(g)=S_n(g^4), degree = 4·9 = **36 for EVERY n**. At n=16 the 36 bad-g are EXACTLY the mod-p roots of this fixed integer poly (verified: g^4 of bad-g = the 9 roots of S_16 mod p). A degree-36 poly has ≤36 roots mod p ⟹ **B(n,p) ≤ 36 UNCONDITIONALLY (degree bound)**, with B<36 only at root-collision primes (disc(R_n)≡0, the DOWN-deviations). ⟹ at n=16 the floor is UNCONDITIONALLY SAFE: no up-deviation is possible, deviations are only DOWN.
**(4) THE ENTIRE RESIDUAL (crisp).** Does the bad-locus stay a FIXED degree-36 integer polynomial R_n for all n, or does the "adjacent/7th-type" agreement pattern (bandcheck found it REALIZABLE at n=32, p=97) contribute p-DEPENDENT EXTRA bad-g beyond R_n's 36 (a genuine UP-deviation B>36)? Mechanism: each agreement pattern A gives a consistency determinant Δ_A(g)∈Z[ζ_n][g]; the 6 allowed types give R_n (deg 36); the adjacent type gives Δ_adj(g). If Δ_adj≡0 identically (never isolated) ⟹ B≤36 always ⟹ FLOOR CLOSES UNCONDITIONALLY. If Δ_adj has isolated roots ⟹ up-deviations at primes p|Res(Δ_adj, ...) ⟹ need those primes < n^4 (a height bound on Δ_adj, the ADJACENT determinant, NOT on disc).
**(5) DECISIVE COMPUTATION:** B(32,97) vs B(32, generic good prime). If B(32,97) ≤ 36 ⟹ no 7th-type contribution to count ⟹ strong evidence floor closes. If B(32,97) > 36 ⟹ up-deviations real (but 97 < n^4) ⟹ bound adjacent-determinant primes. (Running in all-angles workflow w7396kwvb computation cluster + refutation search.)
**META:** caught my OWN TARGET-1 framing as wrong (disc primes exponential) — the right target is the degree/UP-vs-DOWN question, which at n=16 CLOSES the floor unconditionally. Genuine sharpening. CAMPAIGN L1-L125.

## L142 (NEW framing: sub-Gaussian bound = OFF-DIAGONAL Gauss-sum cancellation over BALANCED tuples = a Gauss-sum-WEIGHTED VINOGRADOV mean value mod t; exact value pinned conditional C=√2) 2026-06-21

  Σ_{b}|η_b|^{2K} = (t/t^{2K}) Σ_{(a_i,a'_j): Σa_i ≡ Σa'_j mod t} ∏_i G'_{a_i} ∏_j conj(G'_{a'_j}).

Unweighted Vinogradov is proven (Bourgain-Demeter-Guth decoupling); the Gauss-sum phase WEIGHTING should give EXTRA cancellation (the phases are Stickelberger). The OBSTRUCTION = 2-POWER-order Gross-Koblitz phase resonance (Fermat): at specific balanced tuples the 2-adic Gross-Koblitz phases ALIGN (no cancellation); the ODD part of t adds generic-Weil-phase characters that restore cancellation. So the wall = "off-diagonal Stickelberger-phase Gauss-sum products over the Vinogradov system mod t cancel for thin (β≥4) t" — a multilinear Gauss-sum cancellation = the Paley last-half-power, in a genuinely new (Vinogradov-weighted) form. NOTE memory "decoupling=wrong-norm" applies to the PERIOD directly; here decoupling is at the BALANCED-TUPLE/Vinogradov level (the right object) with Gauss-sum weights (the new lever). exact.js assault running. ## L144 (CORRECTION to L143 + LITERATURE VERDICT: 2112.13886 CONFIRMS the Weil-vacuity wall (does NOT break it); K=2 is trivial Parseval; corpus 53/56 irrelevant, 0 faces moved) 2026-06-21
**CORRECTS L143's over-optimism** (caught by the litmine deep-read, honesty discipline held). Full reading of 2112.13886 (Garcia-Lorenz-Todd "Moments of Gaussian Periods and Modified Fermat Curves"):
- Their 4th moment is computed via HASSE-WEIL on a modified Fermat curve, but it is a **p²-SCALE / THICK-FIELD statement** (d=3: leading (2/9)p², error ≤8p^{3/2}), governed by p NOT n. = the FULL-FIELD/thick moment, the WRONG regime. The curve-point-count's main term IS the count for 0-dimensional μ_n ⟹ **Hasse-Weil VACUOUS at prize thinness** — a clean EXTERNAL CONFIRMATION of our in-tree `_AvJ_T2WeilDegreeVacuous` / [[issue444-Wr-excess-onset-threshold]] (μ_n 0-dim ⟹ Weil vacuous).
- Their fixed-k V₄=3p(n-1)-n³ gives the Wick constant 3 only after dividing by field size = essentially PARSEVAL/TRIVIAL at K=2. So **the "K=2 sub-Wick" is NOT a meaningful partial** (the moment ladder is only nontrivial at K≥log q, which the paper never touches). L143's "rigorously proves our K=2 + method extends" was OVER-CLAIMED.
- The Fermat-curve/Jacobi-sum route IS the Weil route; at moment 2K you need Hasse-Weil on a (2K-2)-dim Vinogradov variety whose error p^{dim/2} SWAMPS the main term in the prize regime = the SAME Weil-vacuity wall. So F2-via-Fermat-variety RE-ENCODES the wall (gives an explicit computable variety) but does NOT crack it — it reduces to the known monodromy/horizontal-flatness open core (the geometric phase cancellation, NOT Weil magnitude).

4. **2112.05441 "Equidistribution of exponential sums indexed by a subgroup of fixed cardinality" [THIN, rel 6]** — Deligne equidistribution of Gauss-period sums at FIXED d; limiting measure = Haar-pushforward on a torus (hypocycloid). Confirms equidistribution but FIXED d (small), distributional not sup-norm.

The sub-Gaussian/o(√x) mechanism, distinct from moment-ladder Wick; thick (full character), transfer to subgroup unproven.

## L149 (SHARP: E_2=3n²-3n EXACT (Wick, p-INDEPENDENT even thick β<3) ⟹ W_2=0; the K=2 energy has ZERO sum-product excess; BGK wall = CUMULATIVE growth of W_K from 0(K=2) to saddle K~log p) 2026-06-21

This is why low-K (Weil/Fermat-curve K=2) results are vacuous for the prize (they see W_2=0, the trivial part) — the prize lives at K~log p where the cumulative wraparound could (but empirically doesn't) blow up.

The Fermat blowup = the step ratio EXCEEDS (2K+1)n at K~v_2. For non-Fermat thin, does the step stay sub-Wick to K~log p? = the exact recursive form of the wall (memory issue444-saddle-K-diagnostic K_max~n^0.77). ## L150 (CLEANEST WALL FORM — the STEP-RATIO recursion: prize ⟺ ρ_K=(A_{K+1}/A_K)/((2K+1)n) < 1 to saddle; ρ_K monotone-decreasing peaking at ρ_1≈Parseval<1 for thin non-Fermat; Fermat CROSSES 1 — exact separator) 2026-06-21
NEW exact reduction via the moment STEP RATIO. A_K=avg_{b!=0}|η_b|^{2K}; R(K)=A_K/((2K-1)!!n^K) (the sub-Gaussian ratio, R(K)≤1 ⟺ prize). KEY ALGEBRA: R(K+1)=R(K)·ρ_K where **ρ_K = (A_{K+1}/A_K)/((2K+1)n) = step/Wick-step**, and R(1)=(p-n)/(p-1)<1 EXACTLY (Parseval). So **R(K)=R(1)·∏_{j<K}ρ_j < 1 for ALL K ⟸ ρ_K<1 for all K.** The prize REDUCES to: the moment step A_{K+1}/A_K never exceeds the Wick step (2K+1)n, to the saddle K~½ln p.
**EXACT SEPARATOR (verified):**
- THIN NON-FERMAT: ρ_K < 1 for ALL K, MONOTONE DECREASING, peaking at ρ_1≈0.96-0.97 (=Parseval, the largest) then falling (n=16: 0.94,0.88,0.82,0.77,0.72,...; n=32: 0.97,0.94,0.91,0.90,0.89,0.86,... all <1 past saddle). p=786433,114689,1179649 all ρ_K<1 ∀K. ⟹ R(K)<1 ⟹ PRIZE holds.
- FERMAT (p-1=2^k): ρ_K CROSSES 1 immediately, peaks 1.47(n=32)/2.77(n=64) — the blowup. ρ_K>1 at K=1..6.
**THE WALL, now in recursion form:** prove ρ_K<1 to the saddle for thin non-Fermat. Equivalently R(K) is DECREASING (and empirically LOG-CONCAVE: ρ_K itself decreasing). Since the MAX is ρ_1≈Parseval<1, a proof that ρ_K≤ρ_1 (monotone) would give the prize from the trivial K=1. The Fermat resonance = ρ_K>1 at K~v_2 (the 2-adic carry inflates the step); the odd part must keep ρ_K<1. THIS IS THE SHARPEST, MOST-PROVABLE FORM: a 1-parameter recursion inequality, separating thin-non-Fermat (prize) from Fermat (blowup), exactly. = step-ratio/saddle-K diagnostic (memory K_max~n^0.77) in clean ρ_K<1 form. ## L154 (PHASE-AWARE REFRAME: η_b empirically an INDEPENDENT GAUSSIAN field N(0,n) with SUB-Gaussian tail; sup M=0.70-0.80·√(2n ln p); the wall = prove the Gaussian/extreme-value tail (phase-aware), NOT the energy (barriered) — the new tools target the TAIL) 2026-06-21
Tested whether the Gauss periods η_b (as a function of b) have the random-multiplicative-chaos structure the new tools (2301.04390, 2509.19067) exploit. RESULT — η_b is empirically an INDEPENDENT real GAUSSIAN field:
- Tail P(|η|/√n > t) = real-Gaussian erfc(t/√2) to ratio ~1.0 for t≤2.5 (n=16,32 p=786433); at t=3 ratio 0.48(n=16)/0.66(n=32) = THINNER than Gaussian (SUB-Gaussian tail).
- corr(|η_b|,|η_2b|) = 0.07(n=16)/0.03(n=32) ≈ 0 (INDEPENDENT, the chaos regime).
- sup M/√(2n ln p) = 0.70(n=16)/0.80(n=32) < 1 (sup BELOW Gaussian extreme-value √(2n log N), N=p-1).
**REFRAME (the right attack with the new tools):** the prize M ≤ √(2n ln p) = the EXTREME VALUE of N=p-1 independent N(0,n) Gaussians. The wall is NOT "bound the energy E_K" (phase-BLIND, proven α=1 barrier L153) but "prove η_b is a SUB-GAUSSIAN Gaussian field" = the large-deviation/extreme-value TAIL P(|η_b|>t√n) ≤ Gaussian. The new tools are PHASE-AWARE TAIL methods (NOT energy): 2301.04390 = better-than-√ via critical multiplicative chaos (controls the DISTRIBUTION/tail); 2509.19067 Rademacher = sub-Gaussian high-moment TAIL for ±1 mult functions. Deploy them on the TAIL, where they beat √, not the energy where they're barriered.

## L177 (D2 metaplectic quadratic-phase: phase-aware effect is REAL (quadratic twist reduces sup to 0.73-0.86×M) BUT b-sum-annihilation HOLDS for the 2nd moment (Σ_b|Θ_c|²=pn-n² unchanged, c-phase b-independent) ⟹ NEW-IDENTITY not break; reduces) 2026-06-21
Tested D2 (the most structurally-promising untried direction, metaplectic theta-lift Θ_c(b)=Σ_{x∈μ_n}ψ(bx+cx²), claimed to evade b-sum-annihilation via the quadratic phase). HONEST NUANCED RESULT:
- **The quadratic twist GENUINELY reduces the sup:** for c≠0, max_b|Θ_c| = 0.73-0.86 × M(linear) (n=16 p=12289: c=7→0.808; n=32: c=7→0.727). So completing the square with ψ(cx²) makes the period cancel MORE — a real phase-aware effect, NOT a reparametrization. The quadratic Gauss weight is doing genuine cancellation.
- **BUT b-sum-annihilation STILL HOLDS for the 2nd moment:** Σ_b|Θ_c(b)|² = pn-n² EXACTLY (= the linear Parseval, unchanged). Reason: the c-phase ψ(cx²) is CONSTANT IN b, so |Θ_c(b)|² = Σ_{x,y}ψ(b(x-y))ψ(c(x²-y²)) and the b-sum still forces x=y, killing the c-dependence. The quadratic phase does NOT survive the b-summation in the second moment.
**VERDICT: D2 is a NEW-IDENTITY (quadratic completion reduces the sup by a constant factor 0.73-0.86), NOT a wall-break.** It REDUCES: the moment method on Θ_c gives the SAME bound as on η_b (identical Parseval), so it routes to the same wall. CRUCIAL STRUCTURAL LESSON: this PRECISELY confirms why L168's b-sum-annihilation is robust — even a quadratic phase, being b-INDEPENDENT, gets annihilated in |Θ_c(b)|². To evade b-sum-annihilation you'd need a phase that DEPENDS ON b nontrivially (b-coupled), which the metaplectic linear-in-b + quadratic-in-x structure does NOT provide. This sharpens the no-go: ANY phase ψ(f(x)) with f independent of b is b-sum-annihilated; the wall requires the SUP (a per-b, b-coupled quantity).
**The OTHER 2 untried (D1 p-adic squeeze, D3 Krein) under test (workflow w12ul4lku).** D1 (integer p-adic squeeze on W_K) is the one that does NOT use phase at all (integer valuation), so it's the genuinely-different mechanism still live. CAMPAIGN L1-L177.
